The Three Perceptions: Conditions or Parts of Assent?
Disagreement on conditions vs. parts of assent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the philosophers' and later logicians' views on the role of the three perceptions in assent and explain the consequence for the self-evidence of assents.

Core Idea
The dispute over conditions or parts is verbal but affects whether assent can be self-evident.

This passage delves into a foundational debate in Islamic logic: are the conceptions of subject, predicate, and relation external conditions for assent, or are they internal parts? Both schools agree they are necessary, but the difference has a real consequence for when an assent counts as self-evident. The commentaries by al-Attar and Abd al-Hakim further explore the verbal nature of the dispute.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two schools
Locate the two positions: the philosophers (hukama) and the later logicians (muta'akhkhirin). Note their agreement that the three perceptions are needed.
2
Contrast 'condition' vs 'part'
Philosophers call the perceptions 'conditions' (shurut) external to assent; later logicians call them 'parts' (shutur) internal to assent. Understand the distinction: a condition is necessary but not constitutive, a part is constitutive.
This distinction is crucial for the definition of assent itself.
3
Derive the implication for self-evidence
If perceptions are parts, then for assent to be self-evident, all its parts must be self-evident. If they are mere conditions, only the judgment (hukm) need be self-evident. See the passage: 'assent according to the later scholars is not self-evident unless all its parts are self-evident...'
4
Analyze the commentaries
Al-Attar and Abd al-Hakim argue the dispute is verbal. They show that regardless of the interpretation, the purpose of logic—finding paths to knowledge—remains unchanged. Abd al-Hakim uses an analogy of a form to unify the perceptions into a single real thing.
This step helps see why the dispute does not affect the core logical project.
5
Apply to an Islamic science
Consider a legal ruling derived from a clear text: Is the assent self-evident? The answer depends on whether you consider the perception of the text's chain and meaning as parts or conditions of the assent to the ruling.
This shows the practical relevance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثانيها : أنَّ التَّصوراتِ الثَّلاثةَ؛ وهي تصوُّرُ الطَّرفين، والنسبةُ؛ شروط في وجودِهِ، وصحته خارجة عنه عند الحكماء، وشطور داخلة فيه عند المتأخرين. ثالثها : أنَّ الحكم نفْسُ التَّصديقِ عند الحكماء، وجزؤه على مذهب المتأخرين، فتحصَّلَ أنَّ المذهبَيْن يتّفقان على أنَّ التَّصوراتِ الثَّلاثةَ مُحتاج إليها في التصديقِ، لكنَّ الاحتياج إليها على أنَّها شروط عند الحكماء، وشطور عند المتأخرين . واعلَمْ أنَّ فائدةَ الخلافِ الَّتي تنبني عليهِ أَنَّ التَّصديق عند المتأخرين لا يكون بديهيا إلَّا إذا كانَتْ أجزاؤه كلُّهَا بديهيَّةٌ، وعند الحكماء يكفي في بداهيه كونُ الحكم فقط بديهيا، وإنْ كانَتِ الأطرافُ نظريَّة . العطار: في ضَمِّهَا إلى الحكم وجعل المجموع قسماً واحداً مِنَ العِلْمِ مُسَمّى بالتصديقِ؛ لأنَّ هذا المجموع ليسَ لَهُ طريق خاص، فَمَن لاحظ مقصودَ الفَنِّ، أعني : بيانَ الطَّرِقِ الموصلة إلى العِلْم لم يلتبس عليهِ أنَّ الواجب في تقسيمه ملاحظة الامتياز في الطُّرقِ، فيكونُ الحُكْمُ أحد قسميه المسمى بالتصديقِ، لكنَّهُ مَشروط في وجودِهِ إلى أمورٍ متعدّدةٍ مِن أفرادِ القسم الآخرِ ا.هـ. ، قال عبد الحكيم : وَلِقَائِل أن يقول : إِنَّ ذلك الإدراك لكونه متعلقاً بالنسبة المتعلقة بالطَّرفين من حيثُ إِنَّهَا الةٌ لِمُلاحظتها بمنزلة الهيئة للشرير المحصلة للأمر الواحِدِ الحقيقي، فَكَمَا أَنَّ الحاصل في الخارج أنَّ الفعل لم يتعلَّق إلا بالهيئة؛ فكذلك الحاصل بعد الحجَّةِ هو المجموع، وإذا كان الاكتساب مُتعلّقاً بالإدراك المذكور، كما أنَّ مُتَعلِّقَهُ، أعني: النِّسبة الخبريَّةَ، بمنزلة الهيئة للقضيَّةِ، بِسببها صارَ الكُلُّ، أعني : الطَّرفَيْنِ والنِّسبة؛ أمراً واحداً حقيقيًّا مُغَايراً لِكُلِّ واحدٍ من الطَّرفين والنّسبة، مع أنَّ الحاصل بعد الطَّرفين ليس إلا النسبة، فَكَما جعلُوا الطَّرفين والنّسبة أجزاء مِنَ المعلوم؛ فكذلكَ العِلْم، وما وجهُ مُخالفةِ العِلْمِ بالمعلوم وجعل الأمور المذكورة شرطاً في الأوَّلِ وشَرطاً في الثَّاني، وأنتَ بعد إحاطتِكَ بما قُلْنَا؛ ظهرَ لكَ أَنَّ النّزاعَ في التصديقِ لفظي، فَمَنْ نظر إلى أنَّ الحاصل بعد الحجّةِ ليس إلا الإدراك المذكورُ ; قالَ ببساطته، ومن نظر إلى أنَّ الإدراك المذكور بمنزلة الجزء الصوري، والحاصل بعد إقامة الحجة إدراكاً واحدٌ متعلّق بالقضيَّةِ ; قالَ بتركبه، ومن نظر إلى أنَّهُ لا يكفي في التَّصديقِ مُجرَّدُ الإدراكِ المذكور، بل لا بُدَّ فيهِ مِن نسبة المطابقة بالاختيار، وإلا لكان إدراكاً تصوريًا مُتعلّقاً بالقضيَّةِ مُسمَّى بالمعرفةِ; قالَ : إنَّه إدراك معروض للحُكم ; سواء قلنا إنَّه الإدراك المذكورُ أو مجموع الإدراكاتِ الثَّلاثِ، فيصح تقسيم العِلْم إلى التّصورِ والتَّصديق بأي معنى تريدُ فيهِ، وأَمَّا النَّظَرُ إلى مقصودِ الفنّ; أعني : بيان طُرُقِ الاكتساب ; فَلَا يرجح شيئاً من ذلك; لتفرُّدِ التصديق على جميعِ التقادير بالكاسب; إما باعتبار نفسه أو باعتبار جزئه، فتدبر ا.هـ.
Second: The three perceptions—which are the conception of the two extremes and the relation—are conditions for its existence and soundness external to it according to the philosophers, and are parts internal to it according to the later scholars. Third: That the judgment is itself assent according to the philosophers, and a part of it according to the later scholars. So it follows that the two schools agree that the three perceptions are needed in assent, but the need for them is as conditions according to the philosophers and as parts according to the later scholars. And know that the benefit of the disagreement built upon it is that assent according to the later scholars is not self-evident unless all its parts are self-evident, while according to the philosophers it suffices for its self-evidence that the judgment alone be self-evident, even if the extremes are theoretical. Al-Attar: Regarding including them with the judgment and making the whole one division of knowledge called assent, because this whole has no specific path. Whoever considers the purpose of the discipline—namely, the statement of the paths leading to knowledge—will not be confused that the obligation in its division is to observe the distinction in the paths, so the judgment is one of its two divisions called assent, but it is conditioned in its existence by multiple matters from individuals of the other division. End quote. Abd al-Hakim said: An objector may say that that perception, because it is related to the relation related to the two extremes in that it is an instrument for observing them, is like the form for the [؟] procuring the single real thing. Just as the result externally is that the act is only attached to the form, so also the result after the argument is the whole. And if acquisition is related to the mentioned perception, just as its object—namely the predicative relation—is like the form for the proposition, by which the whole—namely the two extremes and the relation—becomes a single real thing distinct from each of the two extremes and the relation, despite that the result after the two extremes is only the relation. So just as they made the two extremes and the relation parts of the known, so also knowledge. And what is the basis for opposing knowledge to the known and making the mentioned matters a condition in the first and a condition in the second? And after you have encompassed what we said, it appears to you that the dispute in assent is verbal. For whoever considers that the result after the argument is only the mentioned perception says it is simple; whoever considers that the mentioned perception is like the formal part and the result after establishing the argument is a single perception related to the proposition says it is composite; and whoever considers that mere mentioned perception is not sufficient in assent, but rather there must be in it the relation of correspondence by choice, otherwise it would be a conceptual perception related to the proposition called cognition, says that it is a perception subject to judgment. Whether we say it is the mentioned perception or the total of the three perceptions, the division of knowledge into concept and assent is valid with any meaning you intend. As for considering the purpose of the discipline—namely the statement of the paths of acquisition—it does not prefer any of that, because assent is unique on all suppositions in being acquired, either by virtue of itself or by virtue of its part. So ponder. End quote.
Source pages p. 113

Commentary
This passage is a definitional and epistemological discussion of the nature of tasdiq (assent) and the role of the three perceptions (conception of subject, predicate, and relation) in it. The author presents two positions: the early philosophers (hukama) hold that the three perceptions are conditions (shurut) for the existence and soundness of assent but are external to it, while the later logicians (muta'akhkhirin) hold that they are parts (shutur) internal to assent. Both agree the perceptions are needed, but the disagreement affects whether assent can be self-evident (badihi). For the later scholars, all parts must be self-evident for the whole to be self-evident; for the philosophers, only the judgment needs to be self-evident. Al-Attar's commentary expands on the verbal nature of the dispute, arguing that the disagreement is about how to analyze the relation between the perceptions and judgment. He cites Abd al-Hakim, who uses the analogy of a form (hay'a) to explain that the three perceptions contribute to a unified cognition. The passage concludes that regardless of the interpretation, the division of knowledge into concept (tasawwur) and assent (tasdiq) remains valid, and the dispute does not affect the purpose of logic, which is to identify the paths to knowledge.

تصديق
شرط
شطر

When is Assent Called Assent?
Author explains the prayer analogy for assent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between conditions of soundness and conditions of existence in the context of assent (tasdiq) using the prayer analogy from the passage.

Core Idea
Assent, like prayer, can be defective in conditions but ceases to exist if a pillar is missing.

This passage explores a key disagreement in Islamic logic: when is assent (tasdiq) still called assent? The author uses an insightful analogy with prayer (salat). For the philosophers, missing a condition like purification yields a defective prayer, but it is still called prayer. For the later logicians, missing a pillar like a rak'ah means the prayer does not exist. You will examine how this analogy applies to the conditions of assent and understand the difference between conditions of soundness and conditions of existence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
The passage contrasts the philosophers (al-hukama') who say assent can be called 'valid' even if some conditions are lacking (called 'defective assent'), with the later logicians (al-muta'akhkhirun) who say it is not called assent unless all parts are present.
2
Analyze the prayer analogy
The author draws an analogy: prayer is still called prayer if a condition like purification is missing (defective prayer), but if a pillar like a rak'ah is missing, it is not called prayer at all because its existence depends on all parts.
Conditions of soundness vs. conditions of existence.
3
Apply analogy to assent
Question: Are the three perceptions (conception of subject, predicate, and relation) conditions of soundness or conditions of existence for assent? The passage later argues they are conditions of existence.
4
Evaluate the analogy's fit
The passage raises an objection: if perceptions are conditions of existence, then assent cannot exist without them at all, so calling it 'defective' is invalid. Consider whether the analogy perfectly maps.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والحكم: إما إدراك، أو فِعْل. الدسوقي: وذكر بعض الأشياخ فائدةً أُخرى وهي أنَّه على مذهب الحكماء يُقالُ لَهُ: تصديقٌ، وإن اختلَّ بعضُ الشُّرُوط، غاية الأمر أنَّهُ عند الاختلال يُقالُ له : تصديق فاسد، وعلى مذهب المتأخّرينَ ; لَا يُقالُ له تَصديق إلَّا إذا وُجِدَت الشُّطور، فإن اختلَّ شيءٌ منها ; فَلَا يُقالُ له تصديق، نظير ذلكَ الصَّلاة، فإنَّهُ يُقال لها : صلاة عند فقدِ شرطها كالطَّهارة، غاية الأمر أنَّهُ يُقالُ : صلاةٌ فاسدة؛ لِفَقْدِ شرط الصحة، ولا يُقالُ لها : صلاةٌ عندَ فَقْدِ شطرٍ من شطورِهَا ; أي: ركن من أركانها ; لِعَدمِ وجودها ; إذ وجودها لا يتحقق إلا يتحقق جميع أجزائها، كذا قيل. وفيهِ : أَنَّهُ إِنَّما يصح كونه تصديقاً فاسداً عند الحكماء عندَ فَقَدِ الشروط أن لو كانتِ التَّصورات شروطاً في صحتِهِ كما في الصَّلاةِ، مع أنَّها شروط لوجودِهِ، فَلَا يتأتّى وجوده بدونِها حتَّى يُقالَ : إِنَّهُ تصديقٌ فاسدٌ ; لأنَّ الحكم بالشَّيء – أو على الشَّيء – فرع عن تصوره، فلا يتأتى إدراك أنَّ النِّسبة التي بينَ الشَّيئين واقعة أو غيرُ واقعة إلا بعد تصوُّرِ الشَّيئَيْن، ومُلاحظةِ النِّسبةِ بينَهُمَا، تأمَّلْ. (قَوْلُهُ : وَالْحُكْمُ : إِمَّا إِدْرَاكٌ أَوْ فِعْل ) اعْلَمْ أَنَّ المتأخّرينَ قالُوا : إنَّ الحكم فعل مِن أفعالِ النَّفْسِ الصَّادرة عنها بالاختيار، بدليل أنَّ الألفاظ الَّتِي يُعبَّرُ بها عنه تدلُّ العطار: بِبَساطَتِهِ، ومَنْ نظر إلى أنَّ الإدراك المذكور بمنزلة الجزء الصوري، والحاصل بعد إقامة الحجة إدراكاً واحدٌ متعلّق بالقضيَّةِ ; قالَ بِتَركُبِهِ، ومَنْ نَظَرَ إلى أَنَّهُ لا يكفي في التَّصديقِ مُجرَّدُ الإدراكِ المذكور، بل لا بُدَّ فيهِ مِن نسبة المطابقة بالاختيار، وإلا ; لَكَانَ إدراكاً تصوريًا مُتعلّقاً بالقضيَّةِ مُسمَّى بالمعرفةِ ; قالَ : إِنَّه إدراك معروض للحُكم ; سواء قلنا إنَّه الإدراك المذكورُ أو مجموع الإدراكاتِ الثَّلاثِ، فيصح تقسيم العِلْم إلى التّصورِ والتَّصديق بأي معنى تريدُ فيهِ، وأَمَّا النَّظَرُ إلى مقصودِ الفنّ; أعني : بيان طُرُقِ الاكتساب ; فَلَا يرجح شيئاً من ذلك; لتفرُّدِ التصديق على جميعِ التقادير بالكاسب; إما باعتبار نفسه أو باعتبار جزئه، فتدبر ا.هـ. (قَوْلُهُ : وَالْحُكْمُ إِمَّا إِدْرَاكَ أَوْ فِعْلٌ مُرتبط بقوله: وعند متأخري المنطقيين، وفي عبد الحكيم؛ نقل البعضُ أنَّ الإمامَ مُتردّد في كونه إدراكاً أو فِعْلاً، وفعلَيَّةُ
Judgment is either perception or act. Al-Dasuqi: Some teachers mentioned another benefit: that according to the philosophers, it is called assent even if some conditions are lacking; at most, if they are lacking, it is called defective assent. According to the later scholars, it is not called assent unless the parts are present; if any of them is lacking, it is not called assent. Analogous is prayer: it is called prayer when its condition like purification is lacking; at most it is called defective prayer due to lack of a condition of soundness, but it is not called prayer when a part (i.e., a pillar) is lacking, because its existence is not realized except by the realization of all its parts. This has been said. But there is in it [an objection]: that it is only valid that it is defective assent according to the philosophers when conditions are lacking, if the perceptions were conditions of its soundness as in prayer, while they are conditions of its existence. So its existence cannot occur without them to say it is defective assent, because judgment about a thing or upon a thing is based on its conception; one cannot perceive that the relation between two things exists or does not exist except after conceiving the two things and observing the relation between them. Ponder. (His statement: Judgment is either perception or act) Know that the later scholars said that judgment is an act of the soul issuing from it by choice, evidence that the words by which it is expressed indicate... Al-Attar: Its simplicity: whoever considers that the mentioned perception is like the formal part, and the result after establishing the argument is a single perception related to the proposition, says it is composite; whoever considers that mere mentioned perception is not sufficient in assent, but rather there must be in it the relation of correspondence by choice, otherwise it would be a conceptual perception related to the proposition called cognition, says that it is a perception subject to judgment. Whether we say it is the mentioned perception or the total of the three perceptions, the division of knowledge into concept and assent is valid with any meaning you intend. As for considering the purpose of the discipline—namely the statement of the paths of acquisition—it does not prefer any of that, because assent is unique on all suppositions in being acquired, either by virtue of itself or by virtue of its part. So ponder. End quote. (His statement: Judgment is either perception or act) is linked to his statement: And according to the later logicians, and in Abd al-Hakim; Some transmitted that the Imam was undecided about whether it is perception or act, and its act-ness...
Source pages p. 114

Commentary
This passage discusses the nature of hukm (judgment) and its classification as either perception (idrak) or act (fi'l). Al-Dasuqi first relates another 'benefit' of the earlier disagreement: on the philosophers' view, assent can be called valid even if conditions are lacking (like defective prayer without purification), while on the later logicians' view, it ceases to be assent if any part is missing (like prayer without a pillar). He then raises an objection: the analogy fails because the three perceptions are conditions of existence, not soundness, so without them there is no assent at all to even call defective. The passage then quotes the matn statement 'Judgment is either perception or act' and explains that later logicians consider judgment an act of the soul by choice, as indicated by linguistic expressions. Al-Attar adds that the dispute over whether judgment is simple or composite is verbal and does not affect the division of knowledge into concept and assent, which remains valid. The passage concludes with a note that some scholars (like al-Imam) were undecided on whether judgment is perception or act.

Key Terms
حكم (hukm): Judgment
تصديق (tasdiq): Assent
شرط (shart): Condition
ركن (rukn): Pillar
إدراك (idrak): Perception

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does al-Dasuqi object to the prayer analogy for assent?
A) Because prayer is an act of worship, not a mental judgment.
B) Because the three perceptions are conditions of existence, not soundness.
C) Because the philosophers do not accept the analogy.
D) Because the later logicians reject all analogies.

Key Takeaway
The difference between conditions of soundness and conditions of existence determines whether a deficient judgment is still called assent or not.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider the following statement: 'The Prophet is truthful. I understand the concept of Prophet and truthfulness, but I doubt whether the relationship truly holds.' According to the passage, is this assent defective or non-existent? Explain using the prayer analogy.
?
In a theological debate, someone says: 'I have no clear conception of the attributes, so I cannot assent to 'Allah is knowing' at all.' Which view (philosophers or later logicians) would still consider this a form of (defective) assent? Justify with the passage.

What Is Mantiq?
intermediate
7 min
The Nature of Judgment: Perception or Act?
Author explains debate on judgment's nature and resolves it as verbal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why later logicians consider judgment an act of the soul and why the dispute about its composition does not affect the division of knowledge.

Core Idea
Whether judgment is simple or composite, it is always acquired, preserving the division of knowledge.

After discussing the conditions of assent, the passage turns to the fundamental nature of judgment itself: is it a perception (idrak) or an act (fi'l)? Later logicians argue it is an act of the soul by choice, supported by linguistic evidence. Al-Attar then clarifies that the debate over whether judgment is simple or composite is verbal and does not undermine the foundational division of knowledge into concept (tasawwur) and assent (tasdiq). You will follow the reasoning behind these positions and see how they ultimately serve the same purpose.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions on judgment
The matn states: 'Judgment is either perception or act.' The passage notes that later logicians opt for act, while earlier philosophers lean towards perception or see it as a composite.
2
Examine the evidence for act
The passage states that later logicians say judgment is an act of the soul issuing by choice, and the words used to express it indicate that. For example, the imperative 'judge!' implies voluntary action.
They emphasize that judgment is not passive perception but an active commitment.
3
Understand al-Attar's resolution
Al-Attar says the dispute over whether judgment is simple or composite is verbal. Some see it as composite (the three perceptions plus an extra act), others as simple (just the perception itself). But in all accounts, assent is the object of acquisition (kasb) in logic.
The division of knowledge into concept and assent remains valid regardless of the internal structure of judgment.
4
Confirm the practical outcome
Regardless of the view, the goal of logic (bayān turuq al-iktisāb) does not favor one over the other because assent is always the acquired element, either in itself or through its parts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

What Is Mantiq?

Two Views on the Nature of Judgment
Author presents two competing definitions of hukm as idrak or fi'l and identifies the scholarly camps.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two competing views on the nature of hukm (judgment) in Islamic logic and explain the key difference between the early and later schools regarding its definition.

Core Idea
The nature of judgment is debated: early scholars see it as perception, later as an act.

This passage from the Sharh al-Tadhheeb presents a central debate in Islamic logic: is judgment (hukm) a form of perception (idrak) or an action of the soul (fi'l)? Understanding this disagreement is essential for grasping the epistemological foundations of tasdiq. The author not only presents both views but also clarifies the historical scope of the debate.

Guided Path
1
Extract the two definitions of hukm
Read the passage and identify the two definitions: the early scholars define hukm as idrak (perception), and the later scholars define it as fi'l (act). Note the specific examples used: affirmation, negation, positing, removal.
The passage explicitly contrasts these two views.
2
Trace the reasoning for the early view
According to the early scholars, 'judgment is perception' is not taken literally. They argue by introspection: after perceiving the predicative relation, what remains is only the perception that the relation holds or does not hold. This suggests judgment is a form of perception.
Consider how they refute a literal reading of the terms.
3
Identify the specific acts for the later view
The later scholars hold that judgment consists of acts: positing (iqa'), removal (intiza'), affirmation (ijab), and negation (salab). These are all operations of the soul, hence judgment is an act.
Each act corresponds to a type of judgment.
4
Determine the actual parties in disagreement
The author clarifies that the debate is not among later scholars alone, but between the early and later schools. Understand that the commentator's phrasing might suggest otherwise, but the author corrects this misconception.
This is the critical refinement: the divide is historical.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهو على ذلكَ، كَالإيجاب والسَّلبِ والإيقاع والانتزاع، وعليه؛ فهو تحصيل صورة الشَّيء في الذهن . وقال المتقدِّمون : إنَّه إدراكٌ، وَمَا يُعبَّرُ به مِنَ الألفاظ السَّابقة ليس المراد ظاهره لأنَّا إذا رجعنا لوجداننا ؛ علمْنَا أَنَّهُ بعد إدراكِ النِّسبةِ الحكميَّةِ لم يحصل لَنَا سوى إدراكِ أنَّ تلكَ النِّسبةِ واقعة أو ليست بواقعة، ثمَّ إِنْ فُسِّر الإدراك بانتقاش صورةِ الشَّيء في النَّفْسِ ؛ كان انفعالاً، وإنْ فُسّر بالصُّورة الحاصلة؛ كان كيفاً، الحقُّ كما مرَّ ، وقد علمت معنى الفعل والانفعال فيما مرَّ . إذا علمت هذا ؛ فقولُ الشَّارح: (الحكم إمَّا إدراك)؛ أي: وهو ما قاله المتقدّمونَ، وقولُهُ: (أو فعل)؛ أي: وهو قول المتأخرين؛ أي: لأنَّهم قالُوا : إِنَّ الحكم هو الإيقاع والانتزاع والإيجابُ والسَّلْبُ، وهذه أفعال، فليس الخلافُ في كون الحكم فعلاً أو إدراكاً بين المتأخرين فقط كما قد يتوهم من عبارة الشارح، بل الخلافُ فيما بينهم وبين المتقدمين.
It is upon that, like affirmation and negation, and positing and removal, and accordingly it is the acquisition of the image of a thing in the mind. The early scholars said: It is a perception, and what is expressed by the aforementioned terms is not intended literally, because if we refer to our inner experience we know that after perceiving the predicative relation we only obtain the perception that that relation obtains or does not obtain. Then if perception is interpreted as the impression of the image of a thing in the soul, it is a passion, and if it is interpreted as the acquired image, it is a quality. The truth is as has passed, and you have already learned the meaning of act and passion. If you know this, then the commentator's statement: 'Judgment is either a perception' means it is what the early scholars said, and his statement: 'or an act' means it is the statement of the later scholars, because they said: judgment is positing, removal, affirmation, and negation, and these are acts. So the disagreement about whether judgment is an act or a perception is not only among the later scholars as might be understood from the commentator's expression, but rather the disagreement is between them and the early scholars.
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This passage opens by specifying the nature of judgment (hukm) in the context of tasdiq (assent). The author first states that judgment, according to some, is the acquisition of the image of a thing in the mind, using terms like affirmation, negation, positing, and removal. Then it contrasts this with the view of the early scholars (mutaqaddimun) who hold that judgment is a perception (idrak). The author explains that the terms used to describe judgment are not to be understood literally; rather, upon introspection, after perceiving the predicative relation, we only perceive that the relation either obtains or does not obtain. The passage then examines the definition of perception: if interpreted as the impression of an image in the soul, it is a passion (infi'al); if as the acquired image, it is a quality (kayf). The truth is said to be as previously established. The author then clarifies the commentator's (sharh) statement: 'Judgment is either a perception' refers to the early scholars' view, while 'or an act' refers to the later scholars (muta'akhkhirun). The later scholars consider judgment as positing, removal, affirmation, and negation—all acts. Importantly, the author notes that the disagreement is not only among the later scholars; rather, the primary dispute is between the early and later schools. This sets the stage for the subsequent discussion on the composition of tasdiq.

Key Terms
الحكم (al-hukm): Judgment: the mental act of affirming or negating a predicative relation; its nature is debated between perception (idrak) and action (fi'l). [Note: Stable across the tradition, but the debate about its ontological status (idrak vs. fi'l) is a point of contention.]
الإدراك (al-idrak): Perception: the apprehension of a thing's image in the mind; can be interpreted as a passion (infi'al) or a quality (kayf). [Note: In earlier texts, idrak was used broadly; here it is specifically tied to the nature of judgment.]
الفعل (al-fi'l): Act: an operation of the soul, such as positing, removal, affirmation, negation; considered by later scholars as the nature of judgment. [Note: In the context of judgment, fi'l is opposed to idrak; outside logic, fi'l has broader meanings.]

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) A perception (idrak)
C) Both a perception and an action
D) Neither a perception nor an action

Key Takeaway
The debate over whether judgment is perception or act is a foundational disagreement between early and later Islamic logicians, reflecting different epistemological commitments.

Decomposition of Tasdiq: Three or Four Components?
Author explains tasdiq's composition relative to two views on judgment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two views on the nature of judgment and determine the number of components in tasdiq accordingly.

Core Idea
Tasdiq's composition varies: three perceptions + action if judgment is an action, four perceptions if judgment is a perception.

In this passage, the author explains how the definition of tasdiq (assent) depends on a prior question: Is judgment (hukm) an action or a perception? The later scholars (mutakallimun) and the philosophers (hukama') disagreed, and this disagreement affects the very structure of assent. Understanding this decomposition is crucial for analyzing theological concepts like faith (iman) and its obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two views on judgment
Locate the two explicit views: (1) judgment is an action (fi'l) held by later scholars, and (2) judgment is a perception (idrak) held by early scholars and philosophers. The passage states: 'if we accept the statement of the later scholars that judgment is an action... if we accept the statement of the early scholars that it is a perception.'
The terms 'later' and 'early' refer to chronological order in Islamic logic.
2
Determine the composition of tasdiq under each view
If judgment is an action, tasdiq is composed of three perceptions and one action. If judgment is a perception, tasdiq is composed of four perceptions. The passage explicitly states both counts.
The action is considered an additional component beyond the perceptions.
3
Connect to the concept of iman
The passage notes that faith (iman) is a specific instance of tasdiq. Under the action view, iman is obligated and rewarded in its own essence because the action is directly commanded. Under the perception view, obligation and reward relate to the causes of the perception, not the perception itself.
This shows the direct theological implication of the logical debate.
4
Note the scholarly alignment
The later scholars (like al-Imam al-Razi) are unanimous that judgment is an action, while the philosophers (hukama') are certain that it is a perception. The passage mentions al-'Attar and Abd al-Hakim as sources for this classification.
This alignment helps identify which position a given thinker holds.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأُجيب : بأنَّ قولَ الشَّارح : (والحكمُ . . . إلخ) استئناف، فكأَنَّه قال : ثمَّ إِنَّ قُلْنَا بقولِ المتأخّرينَ مِنْ أنَّ الحكم فِعْل؛ فالتَّصديقُ مُركَّب من ثلاثةِ تصورات وفعل، وإنْ قُلْنَا بقول المتقدِّمينَ مِنْ أَنَّهُ إدراكٌ ؛ كانَ مُركَّباً من أربعة إدراكات . (قَوْلُهُ : إِمَّا إِدْرَاكٌ أَوْ فِعْل ينبني على أنَّ الحكمَ فِعْلُ؛ أنَّ الإيمانَ الَّذِي هو فرد من أفراد الحكم، وهو التَّصديقُ المخصوص مُكلَّف به، ومثاب عليه باعتبار ذاته، والعطار الحُكْمِ هو المشهور عن الإمام ..هـ. وظَاهِرُ شرح الأصلِ للرَّازِيِّ أَنَّ المتأخّرينَ يقولون بفعليَّةِ الحُكم، ولا ترديدَ عندَهُم، وأمَّا الحُكماءُ فَجَازِمُونَ بِأَنَّ الحُكْمَ مِن قبيل الإدراك، وقال عبد الحكيم : إنَّه رأي الحكماء جميعهم، والقولُ بتركُبِ التصديقِ قولُ الإمامِ ومَنْ تَبِعَهُ مِنَ المتأخّرينَ.
And it was answered: That the commentator's statement 'And judgment... etc.' is a new beginning, as if he said: Then if we accept the statement of the later scholars that judgment is an action, then tasdiq is composed of three perceptions and an action. And if we accept the statement of the early scholars that it is a perception, then it is composed of four perceptions. His statement: 'Either perception or action' is based on the fact that judgment is an action; that faith, which is an individual of judgment—namely, specific tasdiq—is obligated by it and rewarded for it in its own essence. And al-'Attar: The view about judgment is the famous one from al-Imam... The apparent meaning of the commentary on the original by al-Razi is that the later scholars say judgment is an action, and there is no hesitation with them. As for the philosophers, they are certain that judgment is of the type of perception. And Abd al-Hakim said: It is the view of all philosophers. The statement about the composition of tasdiq is the statement of al-Imam and those who followed him among the later scholars.
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This passage addresses the composition of tasdiq (assent) in light of the two views on the nature of judgment (hukm). The author begins by interpreting the commentator's statement as a new beginning: if we adopt the later scholars' view that judgment is an action (fi'l), then tasdiq consists of three perceptions (tasawwurat) plus one action. Conversely, if we adopt the early scholars' view that judgment is a perception (idrak), then tasdiq consists of four perceptions. The implication is that the number of components in tasdiq changes depending on the ontological status of judgment. The passage then ties this to the concept of faith (iman), which is a specific instance of tasdiq. Under the action view, faith is obligated and rewardable in its own essence because the action is directly commanded. Under the perception view, faith is not obligated or rewarded in its own essence but rather for its causes, such as acquiring premises. The mention of al-'Attar, al-Imam (likely Fakhr al-Din al-Razi), and the philosophers (hukama') clarifies that the later scholars (especially al-Imam) hold the action view without hesitation, while the philosophers unanimously consider judgment a perception. This distinction is crucial for understanding the nature of tasdiq and its role in epistemology and theology.

الحكماء

Tasdiq's composition is either three perceptions plus an action (if judgment is an action) or four perceptions (if judgment is a perception), with direct implications for the nature of iman.

Critique of the View that Judgment is an Action
Author critiques the basis for claiming judgment is an action, citing al-Sayyid and al-Dawani.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the fallacy in arguing that judgment is an action based on the linguistic form of terms, and articulate Dawani's alternative explanation.

Core Idea
Judgment is not an action; it is a perception—the soul's tranquility is an effect, not a deed.

The nature of judgment (tasdiq) is a central topic in Islamic logic. Some scholars mistakenly thought judgment is an action of the soul based on the active verbs used to describe it. In this passage, al-Jalal al-Dawani refutes this view, showing that the linguistic evidence is weak and that the real source of the mistake is a misinterpretation of an extra psychological effect.

Guided Path
1
Identify the position being critiqued
Determine what claim about judgment is under attack. The target is the view that judgment is an action emanating from the soul.
2
Extract the bases for the claim
Al-Sayyid lists two possible bases: 1) the conventional technical meanings of terms like 'attribution' and 'affirmation', and 2) the literal linguistic meanings of those terms.
3
Analyze Dawani's refutation of the first basis
Dawani argues that if the first basis were correct, then terms for 'knowledge' and 'conception' would also imply action, but no one claims that. Therefore, the basis is inconsistent.
4
Analyze Dawani's refutation of the second basis
Dawani says relying on linguistic meanings while ignoring technical conventions is even more far-fetched, so the second basis fails.
5
Identify Dawani's alternative explanation
Dawani proposes that the mistaken view arose from observing an extra psychological effect in tasdiq—the soul's tranquility—and misinterpreting it as an action, whereas it is a passive reception.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قالَ السَّيِّدُ : تَوهَمُوا أَنَّ الحُكْمَ فِعْلٌ مِن أفعالِ النَّفْسِ الصَّادرة عنها ؛ بناءً على أنَّ الألفاظ التي يعبَّرُ بها عَنِ الحُكُم تدلُّ على ذلك، كالإسنادِ والإيقاع والانتزاع والإيجاب والسَّلب وغيرها، والحقِّ أَنَّهُ إدراك .ا.هـ. وتعقَّبَهُ الجلالُ الدَّوَانيُّ في حاشية القطبِ بأنَّ هذا البناء لا يخلو عَنْ بُعْدِ؛ إذْ لو كانَ منشأ وهمهم كونَ تلك الألفاظ بحسب معانيها الاصطلاحية متقدّمة ؛ فالعِلْمُ والتَّصوُّرُ أيضاً كذلكَ معَ أَنَّهُم لم يتوهَّمُوا كونَهُما فِعْلاً، ومثل ذلك يبعد العُقلاء؛ فضلاً الفُضَلاءِ، ولو كانَ منشأ كونها بحسب معانيها اللغويَّةِ دالة على ما هو من مقولة الفعل ; فذلك أبعد، إذ بناء الأحكامِ اللُّغويَّةِ مع الإغماض عن المعاني الاصطلاحية؛ بعيد جدا والظَّاهِرُ أنَّ منشأ وهمهم أَنَّهُم وجدوا في التصديقِ أَثراً زائداً على أثرِ التَّصورِ، وهو اطمئنانُ النَّفْسِ واعترافها، فحسبوا أنَّ ذلك الأمرَ الزَّائِدَ هو فِعْل صادرٌ عن النَّفْسِ ; حتّى يكونَ التَّصوُّرُ السَّاذَج المتعلّق بالنِّسبة خالياً عن هذا الفعل، وهذا الفعل أمرٌ زائدٌ مُنضم إليه، والتَّحقيق أنَّه ليس هناك إلا إدراك مخصوص بخصوص ماهيّتِهِ، وليس للنَّفْسِ هَهُنَا فِعْلُ ; بل قبولُ كيف لا الآثار المذكورة من جنس الوهم.
Al-Sayyid said: They imagined that judgment is an action from the actions of the soul emanating from it, based on the fact that the terms used to express judgment indicate that, such as attribution, positing, removal, affirmation, negation, and others. But the truth is that it is a perception. End quote. Al-Jalal al-Dawani refuted him in his gloss on al-Qutb, saying: This basis is not free from remoteness; for if the origin of their imagination were that those terms in their conventional meanings are predicated [of actions], then knowledge and conception also are similarly [predicated], yet they did not imagine them to be actions. And such a thing would be remote for rational people, let alone the virtuous. And if the origin were that their linguistic meanings indicate what belongs to the category of action, that is even more remote, for constructing linguistic judgments while ignoring conventional meanings is very far. The apparent view is that the origin of their imagination is that they found in tasdiq an additional effect beyond the effect of conception, namely the soul's tranquility and acknowledgment, so they supposed that this additional thing is an action emanating from the soul, so that the bare conception relating to the relation is devoid of this action, and this action is an additional thing annexed to it. But the verified truth is that there is nothing there except a perception specific by the specificity of its essence, and the soul has no action here; rather it is a reception of a quality; indeed the mentioned effects are of the type of illusion.
Source pages p. 116

Commentary
This passage presents a critical discussion of the view that judgment (hukm) is an action. Al-Sayyid (likely al-Sharif al-Jurjani) states that those who claim judgment is an action base their view on the terms used to express it, such as attribution, positing, removal, etc., which seem to denote actions. However, the truth is that judgment is a perception. Al-Jalal al-Dawani then refutes this basis in his gloss on al-Qutb. Dawani argues that the reasoning is weak: if the source of the illusion were that these terms, in their conventional technical meanings, imply actions, then the same would apply to terms like 'knowledge' and 'conception,' yet no one considers those actions. If the source were the linguistic (literal) meanings, that is even more far-fetched, as it would mean ignoring technical meanings. Dawani instead proposes that the source of their illusion is that they observed an additional effect in tasdiq beyond mere conception, namely the soul's tranquility and acknowledgment. They mistakenly thought this extra effect must be an action of the soul, whereas in reality it is simply a specific perception. The soul does not perform an action here; rather it receives a quality. The perceived effects are illusory. This critique reinforces the position that judgment is a perception, not an action.

Key Terms
الوهم (al-wahm): Illusion: a cognitive faculty that can lead to mistaken beliefs; here used to describe the mistaken view that judgment is an action. [Note: In standard logic, wahm is a specific estimative faculty; here it is used broadly for false imagination.]
الاطمئنان (al-ithmi'nan): Tranquility: the additional effect in tasdiq that some mistakenly take as evidence of an action. [Note: This psychological term is not standard in logical works; it appears in theological contexts.]
القبول (al-qabul): Reception: the soul's passive reception of a quality, as opposed to active doing; characterizes perception. [Note: In physics and metaphysics, qabul is contrasted with fi'l; here applied to epistemology.]

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Jalal al-Dawani, what is the true origin of the mistaken view that judgment is an action?
A) The technical meanings of terms like 'affirmation'
B) The linguistic meanings of those terms
C) The observation of an extra effect (tranquility) in tasdiq
D) The authority of the early scholars

Key Takeaway
The claim that judgment is an action is refuted by showing that its linguistic basis is insufficient and that its experiential basis (tranquility) is merely a perceptible effect, not an agentive act.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Simple Conception: Definition and Seven Subtypes
Commentators define simple conception and enumerate its subtypes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define simple conception (tasawwur saadhij) in terms of its genus and differentia, and enumerate its seven species as identified in the commentary.

Core Idea
Simple conception is knowledge devoid of judgment; it is a relative genus with seven species, not a single type.

In this lesson, we explore the definition of simple conception from the commentary on the matn. The commentator clarifies that 'simple' means 'devoid of judgment', and then provides a detailed breakdown of seven types of conception. We will learn to distinguish between conception and assent, and understand how even relational knowledge can remain mere conception. This foundational concept is essential for understanding how knowledge is classified in Islamic logic.

Guided Path
1
Identify the defining characteristic
The commentator glosses 'simple' as 'devoid of judgment'. Simple conception is knowledge without any judgment (hukm) or assent (tasdiq).
This is the core differentia that distinguishes conception from assent.
2
Recognize the seven subtypes
The commentator of Sullam al-Ulum enumerates seven species: four related to single terms (sensation, imagination, estimation, intellection) and three related to propositions (estimation, imagination, doubt).
Conception is a relative genus (jins idafi) covering these seven.
3
Understand the negation in the definition
The definition 'knowledge if it is not an assent related to the relation' negates either the relation or the assent. Assent without relation is impossible.
This covers all cases of conception, including relational knowledge without judgment.
4
Apply to cases of perception
Perception of the subject alone, predicate alone, both together without relation, or both with relation — all are conception as long as no judgment is made.
The relation can exist in the mind without being attended to as a judgment.
5
Distinguish conception from assent
Al-Attar clarifies that assenting knowledge uniquely involves a quality (al-idh'an) that cannot be absent from it, while non-assenting knowledge can have either consideration.
This reinforces the boundary between conception and assent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويقال له : «التَّصور الساذج» . قوله : السَّاذَجُ أي : الخالي عن الحكم. قال شارح سُلَّم العلوم : التَّصوُّرُ السَّاذَجُ إحساسٌ وتَخييل وتوهم وتعقل، وهذه الأربعة متعلقة بالمفردِ، وَوهم وتخيل وشَكٍّ، وهذهِ الثَّلاثةُ مُتعلّقة بالخبر والقضيَّةِ، فالتَّصور نوح إضافي تحتَهُ أنواع سبعةٌ ، ومَنْ زعمَ أَنَّ التَّصوَّرَ نَوعٌ واحِدٌ حقيقي؛ فقد غفلَ عَمَّا عليه الفلاسفةُ. ثمَّ إِنَّ النَّفي في كلام المصنفِ وردّ على مقيَّد بقيدِ؛ أي: العِلم إن لم يكن إذعاناً متعلقاً بالنسبة؛ فالإذعانُ مُقيَّد، وكونُهُ مُتعلّقاً بالنسبةِ قَيْد؛ فالنَّفي صادق بنفي بنفي النّسبةِ والإذعان، وبنفي الإذعان مع بقاء النِّسبةِ، وأما وجود الإذعانِ بلا نسبة؛ فغير معقول، إذ لا توجدُ الصَّفَةُ بِلا مَوصُوفٍ. فقوله: (فإدراك كل واحد من المحكوم عليه وبِهِ؛ تصور فقط) وكذا إدراكهما معاً بلا نسبة، أو مع نسبة. قوله : وَكَذَا إِدْرَاكُهُمَا مَعَاً بِلَا نِسْبَةٍ :أي: بأن يتصوَّرَ في ذهنه معنى الموضوع بقطعِ النَّظرِ عن كونه محكوماً عليه، ومعنى المحمول بقطع النظر عن كونه محكوماً به، وحينئذ؛ فَلَا يلزم من حصول الموضوع والمحمول في الذهنِ حصول النِّسبةِ فيه؛ لأنَّ ذلكَ اللُّزومَ إِنَّما يكونُ إذا لوحظ الموضوع بوصف كونه محكوماً عليه، والمحمول بوصف كونِهِ محكوماً به، وبهذا اندفعَ مَا يُقالُ: إِنَّ كَلامَهُ يقتضي وجود المحكوم عليهِ وَبِهِ من غير نسبةٍ مع أنَّ النِّسبةَ التَّامَّةَ لازمةٌ لوجودِهما في الذهن. قال العطار: اعتبار عدم الإذعان، والأوَّلُ أعمُّ مِنَ الثَّاني بحسب المفهومِ دونَ التَّحقُّقِ ؛ لأنَّ العِلْمَ التصديقي هو العِلْمُ المتكَيّفُ بالكيفية الإذعانيَّة ؛ لا يمكن فيه عدم اعتبار الإذعان ولا اعتبار عدم الإذعان، وغيرُ العِلْمِ التّصديقي يمكن فيه كلٌّ منهما. (قوله : فَقَطْ) راجع لِكُلِّ مِنَ المحكوم عليه والمحكوم به؛ أي: المحكوم عليه فقط والمحكوم به فقط .
And it is called: 'simple conception'. His statement: 'al-saadhij' means: devoid of judgment. The commentator of Sullam al-Ulum said: Simple conception is sensation, imagination, estimation, and intellection; these four relate to the single term. And estimation, imagination, and doubt; these three relate to the report (khabar) and proposition. So conception is a relative genus under which there are seven types. Whoever claims that conception is a single real type has neglected what the philosophers hold. Then the negation in the author's statement is restricted to a qualification, meaning: knowledge if it is not an assent related to the relation. So assent is qualified, and its being related to the relation is a qualification. So the negation applies to the negation of the relation and assent, and to the negation of assent while the relation remains. As for the existence of assent without a relation, it is inconceivable, since an attribute cannot exist without a subject. So his statement: 'Thus the perception of each of the subject of judgment and predicate of judgment is mere conception.' Likewise their perception together without a relation, or with a relation. His statement: 'And likewise their perception together without a relation' means: that one conceives in his mind the meaning of the subject without considering it as subject of judgment, and the meaning of the predicate without considering it as predicate of judgment. At that time, it does not follow from the presence of subject and predicate in the mind that the relation is present, because that following only occurs when the subject is observed with the description of being subject of judgment and the predicate with the description of being predicate of judgment. And by this is refuted what is said: that his speech implies the existence of subject of judgment and predicate without a relation, while the complete relation is necessary for their existence in the mind. Al-Attar said: The consideration of the absence of assent, and the first is more general than the second in terms of concept but not in actuality; because assenting knowledge is knowledge qualified by the assenting quality; it cannot involve consideration of absence of assent nor consideration of absence of assent. Other than assenting knowledge can involve each of them. (His statement: 'only') refers to each of the subject of judgment and predicate of judgment; meaning: the subject of judgment only and the predicate of judgment only.
Source pages p. 124

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the definition of simple conception (tasawwur saadhij). It begins by quoting the matin: 'It is called simple conception.' The commentator immediately clarifies: 'simple' means devoid of judgment (hukm). This is the core of the definition—conception is knowledge without assent (tasdiq).

The commentator then cites the commentator of Sullam al-Ulum, who provides a detailed breakdown. Simple conception is said to encompass four cognitive acts related to single terms: sensation (ihsas), imagination (takhayyul), estimation (tawahhum), and intellection (ta'aqqul). Additionally, three more states—estimation, imagination, and doubt (shakk)—relate to propositions (khabar/qadiyya). Thus, conception is not a single homogeneous type but a relative genus (jins idafi) with seven species. The commentator warns that anyone who thinks conception is one real type has neglected the philosophers' view.

Next, the passage analyzes the author's negation in the definition: 'knowledge if it is not an assent related to the relation.' The negation is restricted (muqayyad) to two possibilities: either the relation itself is absent, or the assent is absent while the relation exists. Assent without a relation is impossible, because an attribute cannot exist without its subject. So the definition covers both scenarios.

The commentator then explains the matin's statement: 'Thus the perception of each of the subject of judgment and predicate of judgment is mere conception.' This includes four cases: perceiving the subject alone, perceiving the predicate alone, perceiving both together without the relation, and perceiving both together with the relation. The key point is that even when both terms are present in the mind with their relation, if the mind does not attend to them as subject and predicate of a judgment, it remains mere conception.

Al-Attar's addition clarifies that assenting knowledge uniquely cannot involve the consideration of the absence of assent, while non-assenting knowledge can involve either consideration. This reinforces the distinction between conception and assent.

Finally, the passage notes that the word 'only' (faqat) in the matin refers back to each of subject and predicate separately, meaning each by itself is mere conception.

All examples in this commentary are drawn from the Islamic intellectual tradition of logic (mantiq), not from secular sources.

Key Terms

المحكوم عليه
المحكوم به
النسبة
الإذعان

Key Takeaway
Simple conception is a relative genus with seven species, all sharing the characteristic of being devoid of judgment; understanding this breakdown is essential for correctly classifying knowledge in Islamic logic.

Objection and Answer on 'Nisba' as a Homonym
Objection that 'nisba' is a homonym and the answer through common usage or contextual indicator.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct the objection that 'nisba' is a homonym and explain the two responses using the concept of qarina.

Core Idea
A homonym can be used in definitions if a contextual indicator specifies the intended meaning.

In the definition of 'ilm, the term 'nisba' (relation) is used. But if 'nisba' is a homonym with multiple meanings, doesn't that invalidate the definition? This lesson walks through the objection and the sophisticated answer from the logicians, showing how common usage and contextual indicators resolve the issue.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
Locate the objector's claim: 'nisba' is applied to three relations – predicative, descriptive, and genitive – making it a homonym, and therefore unusable in definitions without a qualifying context.
The three relations are: (1) nisba hukmiyya (predicative), (2) nisba wasfiyya (descriptive, e.g., in 'rational animal'), (3) nisba idafiyya (genitive, e.g., 'Zayd's slave').
2
Extract the first answer
Notice that the first response denies that 'nisba' is truly a homonym: the predicative meaning is so famous and frequent that it is the literal meaning; the other uses are figurative.
Fame (shuhra) is taken as evidence of literalness (haqiqa).
3
Extract the second answer
Even if we concede it is a homonym, there is a contextual indicator (qarina). Identify the two types of qarina mentioned: semantic (shuhra itself) and verbal (the word 'idh'an', which only makes sense with the predicative relation).
This second answer is the main safeguard: the context ensures the correct meaning is understood.
4
Apply to the definition of 'ilm
Recall that 'ilm is defined as 'the certain assent corresponding to reality'. The word 'assent' (idh'an) only applies to a predicative relation, so the intended meaning of 'nisba' is clearly the predicative one.
This shows how the verbal qarina works in practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهي لا يُقالُ: «إِنَّ النِّسبة كما تُطلَقُ على النّسبةِ الحُكميَّةِ، كذلكَ تُطلقُ عند النِّسبةِ الوَصفيّة والإضافية، فتكونُ منَ الألفاظ المشتَرَكَةِ، تُستعمل في التعريفات». لأنَّا نقولُ : المشهورُ الكثيرُ الاستعمال هوَ الأَوَّلُ؛ على أنَّ الإذعان لا يُتَصَوَّرُ إلا في النِّسبةِ الحُكمِيَّةِ ، فالقرينَةُ تُجَوِّزُه .
الدسوقي
(قَوْلُهُ : الْوَصْفِيَّةِ) أي : كالنِّسبة في الحيوان الناطق، والإضافية كالنسبة في : غلام زيد .
(قَوْلُهُ : وَهِيَ ) أي : الألفاظ المشتركة، وقوله: (لَا تُستعملُ)؛ أي: بدون قرينة معيَّنة للمراد من ذلكَ اللفظ المشترك .
(قَوْلُهُ : الْمَشْهُورُ ... إلخ) أي : والشُّهرةُ مُجوّزة لاستعماله، فهي قرينة معنوية. (قَوْلُهُ : عَلَى أَنَّ... إلخ) هذا إشارة إلى جواب ثانٍ ؛ أي: وإن لم تراع الشُّهرة إِلَخ. السابقة ؛ فالقرينة موجودة، وهي لفظ الإذعانِ ؛ لأنَّ الإذعانَ لا يُتصوَّرُ إلا في النِّسبةِ الحكميَّة، وحينئذ ؛ فهنا قرينة لفظيَّةٌ مُعيّنةٌ للمراد .
(قَوْلُهُ : فَالْقَرِيْنَةُ . . . إِلَخ) أي : وحينئذ ؛ فهناك قرينة معينة للمراد، إما معنويَّة أو لفظية، والقرينةُ مُجوّزة لاستعمال المشترك في التّعريف.
العطار
(قَوْلُهُ : النَّسْبَةِ الْوَصْفِيَّةِ) بالفاء كحيوان ناطق، والإضافية : كغُلامِ زيد، وكلاهما يُسمى نسبة تقييديَّةٌ كما عبر به سابقاً عنهما .
(قَوْلُهُ): المَشْهُورُ الْكَثِيرُ الِاسْتِعْمَالِ) أي : فيكون استعمال لفظ النّسبة حقيقةً في النِّسبة الحُكميَّة، وهي التَّامَّةُ الخبريَّةُ ؛ فلا يكونُ لفظ النِّسبةِ مِن قبيل المشترك، بل هو حقيقةٌ فيها مجاز في غيرها ؛ لأنَّ التَّبادرَ والشُّهرة أمارة الحقيقةِ، وَلَئِنْ سلَّمْنَا أنَّها مِنَ المشترك بناءً على أنَّ بعض معاني المشترك قد يشتهر ؛ نقولُ: محلُّ منع استعمال المشتركِ في التَّعريف ما لم توجد قرينة معيَّنة، وقد وُجدت، وهي إمَّا الشُّهرة؛ فتكونُ القرينةُ حاليّةً، أو لفظ الإذعان؛ لأنَّه لا يتصوَّرُ إِلَّا في النِّسبةِ التَّامَّةِ الخبريَّة ؛ فتكون لفظية .
And it is not said: 'Indeed, the term nisba, just as it is applied to the predicative relation, is also applied to the descriptive and genitive relations, so it becomes one of the homonyms used in definitions.' Because we say: The well-known and frequently used is the first; moreover, assent is inconceivable except in the predicative relation, so the contextual indicator permits it. Al-Dusuqi: (His saying: 'the descriptive') i.e., like the relation in 'rational animal', and the genitive like the relation in 'Zayd's slave'. (His saying: 'and they') i.e., the homonyms, and his saying: 'are not used' i.e., without a contextual indicator specifying the intended meaning of that homonym. (His saying: 'the well-known... etc.') i.e., and fame permits its use, so it is a semantic contextual indicator. (His saying: 'moreover... etc.') This indicates a second answer: i.e., even if fame is not taken into account... etc. the former, then the contextual indicator exists, and it is the word 'assent'; because assent is inconceivable except in the predicative relation, and thus there is a verbal contextual indicator specifying the intended meaning. (His saying: 'so the contextual indicator... etc.') i.e., and thus there is a contextual indicator specifying the intended meaning, either semantic or verbal, and the contextual indicator permits the use of the homonym in definitions. Al-Attar: (His saying: 'the descriptive relation') with 'fa' like 'rational animal', and the genitive like 'Zayd's slave', and both are called a restrictive relation as previously expressed about them. (His saying: 'the well-known and frequently used') i.e., so the use of the word nisba is literal in the predicative relation, which is the complete declarative relation; so the word nisba is not of the category of homonyms, but it is literal in that and figurative in others, because immediate understanding and fame are indicators of literalness. And if we concede that it is a homonym based on the fact that some meanings of a homonym may become famous, we say: the prohibition of using a homonym in definitions applies only when there is no specific contextual indicator, and it exists: either the fame, so the contextual indicator is circumstantial (haliyya), or the word 'assent', because it is inconceivable except in the complete declarative relation, so it is verbal.
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage is a dialectical exchange (naqd wa jawab) regarding the term 'nisba' (relation) used in the definition of 'ilm. The objector claims that 'nisba' is a homonym (mushtarak) because it is used in three types: predicative (hukmiyya), descriptive (wasfiyya) – like the relation in 'rational animal' – and genitive (idafiyya) – like in 'Zayd's slave'. According to the principle that homonyms cannot be used in definitions without a qualifying context, this would invalidate the definition. The answer provides two defenses: First, the predicative sense is the most famous and common usage, so it is the literal meaning; thus 'nisba' is not a homonym but a term used literally in that sense and figuratively in others. Second, even if it is a homonym, there is a contextual indicator (qarina) that specifies the intended meaning. This qarina can be either semantic (al-shuhra, fame) or verbal (the word 'idh'an', since assent only makes sense with a predicative relation). The commentators elaborate: Dusuqi explains that descriptive and genitive relations are called 'restrictive relations' (nisba taqyidiyya). Attar adds that fame (shuhra) as a semantic indicator (qarina haliyya) or the word 'idh'an' as a verbal indicator both suffice to allow the use of the supposed homonym in a definition.

Resolving Ambiguity of 'Nisba' in Logical Definitions
Dassuqi and Attar address the objection that 'nisba' is ambiguous and defend its usage in definition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and apply the two strategies (fame and contextual indicators) used by Dassuqi and al-Attar to resolve the alleged ambiguity of the term 'nisba' in logical definitions.

Core Idea
Fame and context overcome ambiguity: the 'nisba' is not ambiguous because its common usage and the word 'idh'an' specify the judgmental relation.

In defining 'tasdiq', logicians use the term 'nisba' (relation). An objection arises: 'nisba' has three meanings — judgmental, descriptive, and additive — so it is ambiguous and should not be used in definitions. The commentators Dassuqi and al-Attar provide a robust reply, showing that either the term is not ambiguous due to its fame, or if it is, the context (qarīna) resolves the ambiguity. This lesson walks through their reasoning, which is a classic example of how logicians handle potential ambiguity in technical terms.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Objection
Identify the claim that 'nisba' is ambiguous because it applies to three distinct types of relations: judgmental (ḥukmiyya), descriptive (waṣfiyya), and additive (iḍāfiyya). This would make it a mushtarak (ambiguous word) unsuitable for precise definitions.
The three types are exemplified: 'Zayd is standing' (judgmental), 'rational animal' (descriptive), and 'Zayd's slave' (additive).
2
First Answer: Fame as Sign of Literalness
Al-Attar argues that the most famous and frequent usage of 'nisba' is for the judgmental relation. Immediate understanding (tabādu) and fame (shuhra) indicate that this is the literal meaning. Therefore, 'nisba' is not ambiguous but literal for the judgmental relation and figurative for the others.
This is based on the principle that 'immediate understanding and fame are signs of literalness' (al-tabādu wa al-shuhra amārat al-ḥaqīqa).
3
Second Answer: Contextual Indicator (Qarīna)
Even if we grant that 'nisba' is ambiguous, the context in the definition of tasdiq includes the word 'idh'an' (assent). Assent only occurs with a judgmental relation, so 'idh'an' serves as a verbal contextual indicator (qarīna lafẓiyya) specifying the intended meaning.
Alternatively, the fame itself can be considered a contextual indicator of the state (qarīna ḥāliyya), making the usage permissible.
4
Recognize the Types of Qarīna
There are two types of contextual indicators: (1) qarīna ḥāliyya (state-based), such as the widespread recognition of the judgmental meaning, and (2) qarīna lafẓiyya (verbal), such as the word 'idh'an'. Both resolve ambiguity.
This distinction is standard in Islamic logic and usul al-fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لا يُقالُ: «إِنَّ النِّسبة كما تُطلَقُ على النّسبةِ الحُكميَّةِ، كذلكَ تُطلقُ عند النِّسبةِ الوَصفيّة والإضافية، فتكونُ منَ الألفاظ المشتَرَكَةِ، تُستعمل في التعريفات». لأنَّا نقولُ : المشهورُ الكثيرُ الاستعمال هوَ الأَوَّلُ؛ على أنَّ الإذعان لا يُتصَوَّرُ إلا في النِّسبةِ الحُكمِيَّةِ ، فالقرينَةُ تُجَوِّزُه . الدسوقي (قَوْلُهُ : الْوَصْفِيَّةِ) أي : كالنِّسبة في الحيوان الناطق، والإضافية كالنسبة في : غلام زيد . (قَوْلُهُ : وَهِيَ ) أي : الألفاظ المشتركة، وقوله: (لَا تُستعملُ)؛ أي: بدون قرينة معيَّنة للمراد من ذلكَ اللفظ المشترك . (قَوْلُهُ : الْمَشْهُورُ ... إلخ) أي : والشُّهرةُ مُجوّزة لاستعماله، فهي قرينة معنوية. (قَوْلُهُ : عَلَى أَنَّ... إلخ) هذا إشارة إلى جواب ثانٍ ؛ أي: وإن لم تراع الشُّهرة إِلَخ. السابقة ؛ فالقرينة موجودة، وهي لفظ الإذعانِ ؛ لأنَّ الإذعانَ لا يُتصوَّرُ إلا في النِّسبةِ الحكميَّة، وحينئذ ؛ فهنا قرينة لفظيَّةٌ مُعيّنةٌ للمراد . (قَوْلُهُ : فَالْقَرِيْنَةُ . . . إِلَخ) أي : وحينئذ ؛ فهناك قرينة معينة للمراد، إما معنويَّة أو لفظية، والقرينةُ مُجوّزة لاستعمال المشترك في التّعريف. العطار (قَوْلُهُ : النَّسْبَةِ الْوَصْفِيَّةِ) بالفاء كحيوان ناطق، والإضافية : كغُلامِ زيد، وكلاهما يُسمى نسبة تقييديَّةٌ كما عبر به سابقاً عنهما . (قَوْلُهُ): المَشْهُورُ الْكَثِيرُ الِاسْتِعْمَالِ) أي : فيكون استعمال لفظ النّسبة حقيقةً في النِّسبة الحُكميَّة، وهي التَّامَّةُ الخبريَّةُ ؛ فلا يكونُ لفظ النِّسبةِ مِن قبيل المشترك، بل هو حقيقةٌ فيها مجاز في غيرها ؛ لأنَّ التَّبادرَ والشُّهرة أمارة الحقيقةِ، ولَئِنْ سلَّمْنَا أنَّها مِنَ المشترك بناءً على أنَّ بعض معاني المشترك قد يشتهر ؛ نقولُ: محلُّ منع استعمال المشتركِ في التَّعريف ما لم توجد قرينة معيَّنة، وقد وُجدت، وهي إمَّا الشُّهرة؛ فتكونُ القرينةُ حاليّةً، أو لفظ الإذعان؛ لأنَّه لا يتصوَّرُ إِلَّا في النِّسبةِ التَّامَّةِ الخبريَّة ؛ فتكون لفظية .
It is not said: 'Indeed, the term relation (nisba) is used for the judgmental relation just as it is used for the descriptive and additive relations, so it becomes one of the ambiguous words used in definitions.' Because we say: The famous and abundantly used one is the first; besides, assent (idh'an) is only conceivable in the judgmental relation, so the context (qarina) permits it. Al-Dasuqi: His statement: 'the descriptive' means: like the relation in 'rational animal', and the additive like the relation in 'Zayd's slave'. His statement: 'and they' means the ambiguous words, and his statement: 'are not used' means: without a specific context indicating the intended meaning of that ambiguous word. His statement: 'the famous... etc.' means: and fame permits its usage, so it is a contextual indicator (qarina ma'nawiyya). His statement: 'besides... etc.' indicates a second answer: even if fame is not considered as mentioned previously, the context exists, which is the word 'idh'an' because assent is only conceivable in the judgmental relation, and then, here is a verbal contextual indicator specifying the intended meaning. His statement: 'So the context... etc.' means: and then, there is a specific context for the intended meaning, either semantic or verbal, and the context permits using the ambiguous word in definition. Al-Attar: His statement: 'descriptive relation' with a fa, like 'rational animal', and additive like 'Zayd's slave', both are called restrictive relation (nisba taqyidiyya) as previously expressed by him about them. His statement: 'the famous and abundantly used' means: thus the usage of the word 'nisba' is literally for the judgmental relation, which is the complete predicative relation; so the word 'nisba' is not of the category of ambiguous, but rather it is literal for it and figurative for others, because immediate understanding and fame are signs of literalness. And if we grant that it is ambiguous based on the fact that some meanings of an ambiguous word may become famous, we say: the place of prohibition of using an ambiguous word in definition is only when no specific context exists, and it has been found, either fame, so the context is a state indicator (qarina haliyya), or the word 'idh'an' because it is only conceivable in the complete predicative relation, so it is a verbal indicator.
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage is a hashiya (super-commentary) by al-Dasuqi and al-Attar on a sharh that discusses an objection regarding the term 'nisba' (relation). The objection claims that 'nisba' is ambiguous because it is used for three types: judgmental (like 'Zayd is standing'), descriptive (like 'rational animal'), and additive (like 'Zayd's slave'), so it cannot be used unambiguously in definitions. The answer, as elaborated by the commentators, is twofold: (1) The most famous and common usage of 'nisba' is for the judgmental relation; thus it is not ambiguous but rather a literal term for that meaning and figurative for others. (2) Even if one insists it is ambiguous, the context (qarina) clarifies: either the fame itself serves as a contextual indicator, or the word 'idh'an' (assent) in the definition of tasdiq points specifically to the judgmental relation, since assent only occurs in a proposition. Al-Dasuqi explains the subtypes (descriptive and additive) and emphasizes that fame is a sufficient contextual indicator. Al-Attar adds that both descriptive and additive relations are called 'restrictive relation' (nisba taqyidiyya) and argues that fame is a sign of literal priority; if we grant ambiguity, the presence of a context—be it state-based (the hearing of fame) or verbal (the word 'idh'an')—permits the usage. Thus, the objection fails.

Key Terms
نسبة (nisba): Relation; used in three types: judgmental (ḥukmiyya), descriptive (waṣfiyya), and additive (iḍāfiyya). The focus is on the judgmental type in definitions of tasdiq. [Note: Stable term, though in other contexts nisba may refer specifically to grammatical relational phrases.]
حكمية (ḥukmiyya): Judgmental relation; the relation between subject and predicate in a declarative sentence, expressed by the copula.
وصفية (waṣfiyya): Descriptive relation; a relation within a phrase that qualifies a noun, like 'rational animal'.
إضافية (iḍāfiyya): Additive relation; the relation of possessor and possessed in a genitive construction, like 'Zayd's slave'.
مشترك (mushtarak): Ambiguous word; a single lexical item with multiple distinct meanings, requiring context for disambiguation. [Note: Standard term in Arabic lexicology and logic.]
قرينة (qarīna): Contextual indicator; either a state (ḥāliyya) or verbal (lafẓiyya) clue that specifies the intended meaning of an ambiguous expression. [Note: Technically used in usul al-fiqh and logic; stable.]
إذعان (idh‘ān): Assent; the act of affirming or accepting a proposition, which can only occur with a judgmental relation. [Note: Synonym for tasdiq in this context; stable.]

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The word 'idh'an' is always present
B) Immediate understanding and fame are signs of literalness
C) The descriptive relation is more common
D) The additive relation is not a true relation

Key Takeaway
The resolution of the 'nisba' ambiguity demonstrates that logicians rely on usage frequency (fame) and contextual clues to disambiguate terms, preserving the clarity of definitions.

What Is Mantiq?

Defining Necessary Knowledge: Grammatical and Logical Precision
Al-Dasūqī and al-‘Aṭṭār analyze the definition of necessary knowledge and its grammatical-logical issues.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and resolve the logical problem of circularity in defining necessary knowledge by distinguishing between the word and its intended meaning.

Core Idea
A definition must avoid self-reference; grammatical gender can signal a deeper logical shift.

In this passage, al-Dasūqī and al-‘Aṭṭār dissect the definition of necessary knowledge. They uncover a grammatical choice that could lead to a circular definition—a serious logical flaw. Their solution reveals how commentators in the Islamic tradition use both linguistic analysis and logical principles to sharpen definitions. You will learn to spot such issues in other definitions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition being analyzed
Find the phrase 'It is that whose attainment does not depend on reflection and acquisition' in the Arabic. This is the definition of necessary knowledge (al-‘ilm al-ḍarūrī) under scrutiny.
2
Notice the grammatical gender inconsistency
The pronouns and relative pronoun (hiya, allatī) are feminine because they grammatically agree with the word 'ḍarūra' (necessity), even though the intended meaning is the masculine 'ḍarūrī' (necessary). The author chose form over meaning.
Al-Dasūqī explicitly points this out.
3
Detect the circularity problem
If the relative pronoun 'allatī' refers to 'ḍarūra' itself, then the definition defines 'ḍarūra' using 'ḍarūra' as a genus, which is a circular definition (taking the thing as a genus for itself). This is invalid.
Al-‘Aṭṭār raises this objection.
4
Understand the solution
The pronoun must refer to the implied 'form' (ṣūra), which is not explicitly stated but is indicated by 'ḍarūra' as an attribute of knowledge. Also, the conditions of dependency (without it, not attained) and ordering (precedence) refine the definition to avoid circularity and include appropriate cases.
The solution invokes the concept of 'condition of respect' (ḥaythiyya) for relational definitions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهي الدسوقي التي لم يتوقف حصولها على نَظَرٍ وكَسْبٍ . (قَوْلُهُ: وَهِيَ الَّتِي مَا لَا يَتَوَقَّفُ) أي : والضَّرورة بمعنى الضروري: العِلْمُ الَّذِي لا يتوقَّف؛ أي: الصُّورة الحاصلة في العقل التي لا يتوقف حصولها فيه على نظر ... إلخ ، وإنَّما أَنَّكَ الضَّمير وعبَّر بالتي ؛ نظراً لِلّفظِ الضَّرورة لا لمعناها المراد منها، وهو الضَّروريُّ ؛ إذْ لَوْ نظر لِذلكَ ؛ لذكَّرَ الضَّمير والموصول. العطار (قَوْلُهُ : وَهِيَ الَّتِي الضَّمير يعودُ للضَّرورة، والموصول المتبادرُ منه وقوعه على الضَّرورةِ، وهو فاسد ؛ لأدائِهِ لأخذِ الشَّيء جنساً في تعريف نفْسِهِ، ولا محيص عنه إلا بدعوَى وُقُوعِهِ على الصُّورةِ، وهي ، وإن لم تكن مذكورةً؛ لكنَّه يشعرُ بها الضَّرورة الَّتي هِيَ صِفَةٌ لِلعِلْم المفسَّرِ بالصُّورة الحاصِلَةِ عندَ النَّفْسِ، قال عبد الحكيم في تقرير تعريف صاحبِ الشَّمسيَّةِ لِلعِلْم الضَّروريّ بِقولِهِ : وهوَ الَّذي لم يتوقف ... إلخ؛ أي: العِلْمُ بمعنى الصُّورةِ الَّذي لم يتوقف حصوله المعتبر في مفهومِهِ، فَلَا يلزم أن يكونَ للحصولِ حصول، وتعدّيةُ التَّوقُفِ بـ «على» يتضمَّنُ معنى الترتيب؛ فَيُفيدُ قِيدُ التَّوقُفِ أَنَّهُ لولاهُ؛ لَمَا حَصَلَ ، وقَيْدُ التَّرتُبِ التَّقَدُّم، فيؤول إلى معنى الاحتياج، فَبِالقَيدِ الأوَّلِ : دخلَ العِلْمُ الضَّروريُّ الَّذي حصلَ بالنَّظَرِ أيضاً كالعِلْم؛ بأن ليس جميعُ التَّصوراتِ والتَّصديقات بديهيا ولا نظريًّا، وبالقيدِ الثَّاني : العِلَّمُ الضَّروريُّ التَّابِعُ لِلعِلْم النَّظريّ، إذا قُلْنَا : إِنَّهُ ضَروري بمعنى البديهي كَالعِلْمِ بِالعِلْم النَّظريّ ؛ فَإِنَّهُ وإِنْ كانَ يُصدقُ عليهِ أَنَّهُ لولا النَّظُرُ لَمَا حَصَلَ ؛ لكنَّهُ ليسَ مُرتَّباً عَلى النَّظَرِ، بل على العِلْم المستَفَادِ مِنَ النَّظرِ ، فإنَّ المتبادرَ مِنَ التَّرتُبِ ؛ التَّرتُ بِلا واسطةٍ، ثمَّ إِنَّ البديهي والنَّظريّ يختلفان بالنّسبة إلى الأشخاص ، فَرُبَّما يكون نظريًّا لِشخص؛ بَدِيهِيَّا لِأَخَرَ، وبالعكس ، فَقَيدُ الحيثية مُعتبرُ في التَّعريفِ على ما تقرَّرَ مِنْ أَنَّهُ يُعتبرُ في تعريفاتِ الأُمورِ الاعتبارية قيد الحيثية وإن لم نذكر ا.هـ. ملخصاً، لا يُقَالُ: إذا عرف العلم الضروري صار نظريًّا ؛ لاحتياجه للتَّعريفِ، فينتظِمُ قَضيَّتَانِ مُتَناقِضَتَانِ هُمَا ؛ الضَّروريُّ : ما لا يتوقَّفُ ... إلخ ، الثَّانية : الضَّروري يتوقَّفُ؛ لأنَّا نقولُ : لا تَنَاقُضَ لاختلافِ الموضوع، فإنَّ قولنا : الضَّروري يتوفَّفُ... إلخ، المرادُ بِهِ المفهوم
Al-Dasūqī: 'It is that whose attainment does not depend on reflection and acquisition.' (His saying: 'It is that which does not depend') meaning: and al-ḍarūra in the sense of al-ḍarūrī: the knowledge that does not depend; i.e., the form present in the mind whose presence does not depend on reflection... etc. He only used the feminine pronoun and 'allatī' considering the word 'ḍarūra', not its intended meaning, which is 'ḍarūrī'; for if he considered that, he would have made the pronoun and relative masculine. Al-‘Aṭṭār: (His saying: 'It is that which') the pronoun refers to ṭarūra, and the relative prima facie applies to ṭarūra, which is invalid because it leads to taking the thing as a genus in defining itself. There is no escape from it except by claiming that it applies to the form (ṣūra), which, although not mentioned, is indicated by 'ḍarūra' which is an attribute of knowledge interpreted as the form present in the soul. ‘Abd al-Ḥakīm said in explaining the definition of the author of al-Shamsiyya for necessary knowledge by his saying: 'It is that which does not depend... etc.' i.e., knowledge in the sense of the form whose attainment, which is considered in its concept, does not depend; so it is not necessary that attainment has an attainment. The transitive 'alā' includes the meaning of ordering; thus the condition of dependency indicates that without it, it would not be attained, and the condition of ordering indicates precedence, so it amounts to the meaning of need. By the first condition, necessary knowledge that is attained by reflection also enters, such as the knowledge that not all concepts and assents are self-evident nor theoretical. By the second condition, necessary knowledge that follows theoretical knowledge, if we say it is necessary in the sense of self-evident, like knowledge of theoretical knowledge; for although it is true that without reflection it would not be attained, it is not ordered upon reflection, but upon the knowledge obtained from reflection, for the immediate understanding of ordering is ordering without intermediary. Then, self-evident and theoretical differ relative to persons; what is theoretical for one may be self-evident for another, and vice versa. Thus, the condition of respect (ḥaythiyya) is considered in the definition, based on the established principle that in definitions of relational matters, the condition of respect is considered even if not mentioned. End of summary. It cannot be said: 'If necessary knowledge is defined, it becomes theoretical because it needs a definition, so two contradictory propositions arise: necessary is that which does not depend, and necessary depends'; because we say: there is no contradiction due to difference of subject, for our saying 'necessary depends' is intended to mean the concept.
Source pages p. 138

Commentary
This passage is a detailed grammatical and logical commentary on the definition of necessary knowledge (al-‘ilm al-ḍarūrī). Al-Dasūqī first clarifies that the definition 'that which does not depend' refers to knowledge as a form in the mind. He notes a grammatical subtlety: the author used feminine pronouns (hiya, allatī) because the word 'ḍarūra' (necessity) is feminine, even though the intended meaning is 'ḍarūrī' (necessary), which is masculine. Al-‘Aṭṭār then raises a serious logical issue: if the relative pronoun 'allatī' refers to 'ḍarūra' itself, the definition would be circular—defining a thing by taking it as a genus. The solution is to claim that 'allatī' refers to the unmentioned 'form' (ṣūra), which is implied by the word 'ḍarūra' as a property of knowledge. The commentary then cites ‘Abd al-Ḥakīm’s analysis of the definition from al-Shamsiyya, explaining that the dependency condition includes two aspects: (1) without it, the knowledge would not be attained, and (2) the ordering implies precedence and need. These conditions allow certain types of necessary knowledge to be included or excluded. For example, knowledge attained through reflection (like 'not all is self-evident or theoretical') is still considered necessary because its attainment does not depend on reflection in the same way. The passage also addresses the objection that defining necessary knowledge makes it theoretical; the response is that there is no contradiction because the subject differs: one proposition refers to the nature of necessary knowledge, the other to its definition. The cut-off text likely continues the response.

Key Terms
الضَّرورة (al-ḍarūra)
الصُّورة (al-ṣūra)
الحيثية (al-ḥaythiyya)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is it problematic for the relative pronoun in the definition to refer directly to 'ḍarūra'?
A) It would make the definition grammatically incorrect.
B) It would define the thing by itself, leading to circularity.
C) It would imply that necessary knowledge has no definition.
D) It would mix necessity with reflection.

Key Takeaway
A definition of necessary knowledge must be carefully worded to avoid self-reference; the commentators resolve this by interpreting the relative pronoun as referring to the implied 'form' of knowledge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider the definition: 'al-‘ilm al-ḍarūrī is that which does not depend on reflection.' Identify the potential circularity if the relative pronoun refers to 'al-ḍarūrī' and propose a way to avoid it using the solution from the passage.
?
In a Fiqh definition: 'al-ribā is an increase in one of two exchanged items without equality.' Check if there is any self-reference; if so, how would you rephrase to avoid circularity?

What Is Mantiq?
