Resolving the Famous Question on the Subject of Logic
Author resolves a famous question about the subject of logic.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two interpretations of the subject of logic and explain why the absolute interpretation is correct.

Core Idea
The subject of logic is absolute knowledge that leads to unknown knowledge, not specific definitions.

In this passage, the author addresses a classical question about the subject of logic. The issue is whether the subject leads to accidental attributes. By analyzing two possible interpretations, the author refines the definition of logic's subject, showing that it is the absolute conceptual and assertoric knowledge that leads to unknown conceptual and assertoric knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Question
Find the famous question: if the essential accident is necessarily connected in existence, why is its proof required in the science? The answer is that absence of a middle in reality does not mean absence in knowledge.
2
Examine the Two Interpretations
The text considers two meanings for 'the conceptual known' and 'the assertoric known': either the concept (mafhum) of the two knowns, or the referents (afrad) of the two knowns.
3
Analyze the Consequences
If concept, then 'leading' becomes an accidental accident, not studied. If referents, then all specific definitions and proofs would be the subject, which is not the case.
4
Grasp the Resolution
The correct view is to take the referents but absolutely (bi-wajh al-itlaq), i.e., insofar as they lead to some unknown conceptualization or assent, not specific ones.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثُمَّ إِنَّ هَهُنَا سُؤَالاً مشهوراً؛ وهو أَنَّهُ إِذا كانَ العرضُ الذاتيَّة الأولى وهو اللَّاحِقُ للشَّيء لِذاتِهِ؛ يكون بينَ الثَّبوتِ لَهُ، فَلَا يكونُ إثباتُهُ مَطلوباً في العِلْمِ لِومُجُوبِ كَوْنِ المسائل نظريَّةٌ، وأجابوا بأنَّ انتفاء الواسطة في الثبوتِ في الواقع لا يستلزم انتفاء الواسطة في الإثباتِ، أي: العِلمِ بالثبوتِ، فيجوز أن يكون العارضُ لِذاتِهِ غيرَ بَيِّنِ الثَّبوتِ، فيطلب في العلم بالبرهان. (قَوْلُهُ: المَعْلُوْمُ التَّصَوُّرِيُّ ... إِلَخ) إِنْ أُرِيدَ مفهوم المعلومينِ ؛ لَزِمَ أن يكونَ الإيصالُ إلى الأمور المذكورةِ عَرضاً غريباً؛ لأنَّه لا يعرضُ لمفهوم المعلومين بواسطة أمرٍ أخصَّ، واللاحِقُ بواسطة الأمرِ الأخصّ عرض غريب، والأعراضُ الغريبة لا يبحث عنها في العِلم، مثلاً: الإيصال إلى كُنْهِ الحقيقةِ إِنَّما يعرضُ للمعلوم التصوري بواسطة كونه حدًّا، والإيصال إلى المجهول التصديقي إنَّما يعرضُ للمعلوم التصديقي بواسطةِ كَونِهِ حَجَّةً، وإِنْ أُرِيدَ مَا صدق عليه المعلومات؛ أي: أفرادها ؛ لَزِمَ أن تكونَ جميعُ الحدودِ والحجج المستعملة في العلوم موضوع المنطقِ، وظاهرُ أَنَّهُ لا يبحث عن أحوالها، والجواب باختيارِ الشَّقِّ الثَّاني، وأنَّ المراد هذه الماصدقات من حيثُ إِنَّها توصل إلى تصوُّرٍ مَا وتصديقٍ مَا؛ لا إلى تصورٍ أو تصديقٍ مَخصُوص، فَهِيَ مَوضوعُهُ على وجهِ الإطلاقِ والإجمال، وأما الحدود والحجج المستعملة في العلوم؛ فإنَّها توصل إلى تصوّرٍ مَخصوص وتصديقٍ مخصوص، وفي حاشية قول أحمدَ على الفناري: فإِنْ قِيلَ: ليس في المنطقِ مسألةٌ محمولُها الإيصال أو ما يتوقَّفُ عليهِ الإيصال؛ قِيلَ: إذا مُحكِّم على المعلوم
Then there is a famous question here: If the essential accident — that which attaches to a thing due to its essence — is necessarily connected in existence to it, then its proof would not be required in the science because the problems must be theoretical. And they answered that the absence of a mediating cause in reality does not necessitate the absence of a mediating cause in proof, i.e., in knowledge of the existence. So it is possible that the accident attaching to the essence is not evident in its existence, so it is sought in science through demonstration. (His statement: 'the conceptual known... etc.') If what is intended is the concept of the two knowns, then the leading to the mentioned matters would be an accidental accident because it does not attach to the concept of the two knowns by virtue of a more specific matter. And what attaches by virtue of a more specific matter is an accidental accident, and accidental accidents are not investigated in science. For example: leading to the essence of reality attaches to the conceptual known only by virtue of its being a definition; and leading to the unknown assertoric attaches to the assertoric known only by virtue of its being a proof. And if what is intended is the referents (i.e., the individuals) of the two knowns, then all definitions and proofs used in the sciences would be the subject of logic, and it is apparent that it does not investigate their states. The answer is to choose the second option: that what is meant is these referents insofar as they lead to some conceptualization and some assent, not to a specific conceptualization or specific assent. So they are its subject in an absolute and general manner. As for the definitions and proofs used in the sciences, they lead to specific conceptualization and specific assent. And in the gloss of Ahmad on al-Fanari: If it is said: there is no problem in logic whose predicate is the leading or that upon which the leading depends; it is said: if [the leading] is predicated of the known...
Source pages p. 175

Commentary
This passage addresses a famous question concerning the subject matter of logic. It begins by noting that if an accident is essential (attaching due to essence), then its proof seems unnecessary because it is necessarily connected. However, the answer is that while there is no mediating cause in reality (wusta fil-thubut), there may still be one in our knowledge of it (wusta fil-ithbat). Thus we may need demonstration to know it. The passage then comments on the phrase 'the conceptual known' from the text. It considers two interpretations: if we take the concept of the two knowns (conceptual and assertoric), then the attribute of 'leading to unknown things' would be a accidental accident because it attaches only via a more specific notion (like being a definition or proof). If we take the individuals (referents), then all concrete definitions and arguments would be the subject, which is not the case. The solution is to take the referents but not as specific individuals; rather, they are considered absolutely (bi-wajh al-itlaq), i.e., insofar as they lead to some unknown conceptualization or assent, not to a specific one. Thus the subject of logic is the absolute conceptual and assertoric known that leads to unknown knowledge. The passage ends with a note from a gloss on al-Fanari, discussing a potential objection: that no problem in logic has 'leading' as its predicate; the response is that 'leading' is predicated in a certain manner.

Key Terms
المعلوم التصوري
المعلوم التصديقي
الإيصال

D) The acts of leading

Key Takeaway
The subject of logic is the absolute conceptual and assertoric knowledge that leads to unknown conceptual and assertoric knowledge, not specific instances.

The Subject of Logic: Knowns as Means, Not Absolutely
Commentary on the author's definition of the subject matter as the two knowns.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the subject of logic is not all knowns but only those that lead to desired ends.

Core Idea
Logic studies knowns only as means, not as things in themselves.

In this passage, the commentator expands on the author's definition of logic's subject matter. The key move is restricting the scope: logic does not treat every conceptual or assent known, but only those that function as means to further knowledge. This precision is essential for understanding logic's role as a tool.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two knowns
Locate the mention of 'al-ma'lum al-tasawwuri' and 'al-ma'lum al-tasdiqi' in the passage. These are the two types of knowns that logic studies.
2
Find the qualification 'not absolutely'
The passage states 'موضوع المنطق هذان المعلومان لا مطلقا' (the subject of logic is these two knowns, not absolutely). Note the phrase 'la mutlaqan'.
This is the crucial restriction.
3
Understand the respect (al-haythiyya)
The commentator explains that logic considers knowns 'min haythu innahu yusilu' (insofar as they lead). Al-Attar clarifies that 'al-haythiyya' here is for restriction.
This means the subject is defined by a specific aspect.
4
Contrast with other sciences
In other sciences, knowns are studied for their own sake (e.g., physics studies bodies as such). Logic only studies knowns as tools to reach other knowledge.
This distinction separates logic from the sciences it serves.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إذا علمت هذا فقول المصنف المعلوم التصوري أي مطلق المعلوم التصوري الموصل للمطلوب تصوريا كان المطلوب أو تصديقيا فيصدق بالموصل القريب للمطلوب التصوري كالحد وبالموصل البعيد له كالكليات الخمس وبالموصل الأبعد للمطلوب التصديقي تكون ذلك الموصل موضوعا أو محمولا لأنه يبحث في هذا الفن عن الأول بأنه حد مثلا وعن الثاني بأنه جنس أو فصل وعن الثالث بأنه موضوع أو محمول وحينئذ فيكون قول المصنف من حيث إنه يوصل إلى مطلوب تصوري أي أو تصديقي ويكون قول الشارح التصوري بأنه حد أو رسم كان معناه أنه موصل إلى المجهولات التصورية بلا واسطة وقش ا.هـ. وأقول قد يقع الإيصال محمولا كما يقال الحد موصل إلى كنه الحقيقة والرسم موصل لامتيازها عن غيرها مثلا . كالحيوان والناطق مثلا . و المعلوم التصديقي كقولنا العالم متغير وكل متغير حادث . أي موضوع المنطق هذان المعلومان لا مطلقا . الدسوقي كالحيوان أي ومثله غيره من الأجناس وقوله والناطق أي ومثله غيره من الفصول. وقوله مثلا أي ومثل ذلك الموصل القريب كالحد للمطلوب التصوري والموصل الأبعد للمطلوب التصديقي ككونه موضوعا أو محمولا وبهذا تعلم المناسب الإتيان بالواو الداخلة على الناطق لا حذفها كما قيل وأن قوله مثلا له فائدة فلا يستغني عنه بالكاف كما قيل. قوله المعلوم التصديقي أي ومطلق المعلوم التصديقي الموصل للمطلوب التصديقي فيصدق بالموصل القريب كالقياس وبالموصل البعيد كالقضية وقول الشارح كقولنا العالم متغير أي ومثله غيره من الأقيسة وقوله مثلا أي ومثله الموصل البعيد كالقضية. وبهذا ظهر لك أن الشارح صرح في جانب المعلوم التصوري بالموصل البعيد وأدخل بمثلا الموصل القريب وصرح في جانب المعلوم التصديقي بالموصل القريب وأدخل بمثلا الموصل البعيد . قوله لا مطلقا أي لا من حيث ذاتهما كانت موصلة لما ذكر أم لا . العطار قوله كالحيوان والناطق مثلا الكاف لإدخال بقية الحدود التامة ومثلا لإدخال بقية المعرفات قوله لا مطلقا إشارة إلى أن الحيثية هنا للتقييد كقولهم الإنسان من حيث (۱) . (۱) (قوله وأدخل بمثلا ... إلخ) لم يذكر الشارح كلمة (مثلا) في جانب المعلوم التصديقي . ا. هـ. الشرنوبي.
If you know this, then the author's statement 'the conceptual known' means the absolute conceptual known which leads to the desired, whether the desired is conceptual or assenetic. So it applies to the near means to the conceptual desired like the definition, and to the far means to it like the five universals, and to the more distant means to the assenetic desired when that means is a subject or a predicate, because in this art (logic) one investigates the first as being a definition, for example, and the second as being a genus or a difference, and the third as being a subject or a predicate. So then the author's statement, insofar as it leads to a conceptual desired, means also a assenetic desired. And the commentator's statement that the conceptual is a definition or description means that it is a means to conceptual unknowns without intermediary. And I say: sometimes the delivery occurs as a predicate, as is said: the definition leads to the essence of the reality, and the description leads to its distinction from others, for example. 'Like animal and rational, for example.' And the assenetic known is like our statement: 'The world is changing, and everything changing is originated.' That is, the subject of logic is these two knowns, not absolutely. Al-Dusuqi: 'Like animal' meaning and similarly other genera; and his statement 'and rational' meaning and similarly other differences. And his statement 'for example' means similar to the near means like the definition for the conceptual desired, and the more distant means for the assenetic desired like being a subject or a predicate. By this you learn the appropriateness of inserting the conjunction 'and' on 'rational', not omitting it as was said, and that his statement 'for example' has a benefit, so one cannot dispense with it by the kaaf as was said. His statement 'the assenetic known' means the absolute assenetic known which leads to the assenetic desired, so it applies to the near means like the syllogism and the far means like the proposition. And the commentator's statement 'like our statement: the world is changing' means similar other syllogisms; and his statement 'for example' means similar to the far means like the proposition. By this it becomes clear to you that the commentator explicitly mentioned in the aspect of the conceptual known the far means and included by 'for example' the near means, and explicitly mentioned in the aspect of the assenetic known the near means and included by 'for example' the far means. His statement 'not absolutely' means not from the perspective of their essences, whether they lead to what was mentioned or not. Al-Attar: The kaaf in 'like animal and rational, for example' is for including the remaining complete definitions, and 'for example' is for including the remaining definers. His statement 'not absolutely' indicates that the respect (al-haythiyya) here is for restriction, like their saying: 'man from the perspective of ...' (1). (1) (His statement: 'and included by 'for example' ... etc.') Al-Sharnubi says: The commentator did not mention the word 'for example' in the aspect of the assenetic known.
Source pages p. 176

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the earlier classification, focusing on the author's precise wording and the subject matter of logic. The commentator interprets 'al-ma'lum al-tasawwuri' as the absolute conceptual known that leads to any desired, whether conceptual or assenetic. This includes the far means (five universals) and the more distant means (subject/predicate). The commentator then clarifies that logic studies these knowns insofar as they are means, not absolutely. Al-Dusuqi adds that the example 'animal and rational' represents genera and differences, respectively. The inclusion of 'waw' (and) before 'rational' is justified as necessary for enumeration. The discussion then turns to the assenetic known: the near means (syllogism) and far means (proposition). The commentator notes that the author explicitly stated the far means for the conceptual and the near means for the assenetic, but used 'for example' to hint at the other. Al-Attar explains that 'kaaf' (like) and 'mthalan' (for example) serve to include additional items beyond the examples given. The phrase 'not absolutely' means that the subject of logic is not the knowns in themselves, but specifically insofar as they function as means to knowledge. This careful parsing demonstrates the precision required in understanding logical terminology.

Key Terms
المصنف
الشارح
موضوع المنطق
الحيثية

Checkpoint
What does 'la mutlaqan' (not absolutely) mean in the sentence 'موضوع المنطق هذان المعلومان لا مطلقا'?
A) The subject of logic is the two knowns without any qualification.
B) The subject of logic is the two knowns, but not in their essence; only as means to ends.

D) The subject of logic excludes the assenetic known.

Key Takeaway
Logic's subject matter is the two knowns restricted to their function as means, a precision that prevents overreach and clarifies its role as a tool.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
